[{"text": "the VImos Public Extragalactic Redshift Survey", "label": "ORG"}, {"text": "PDF", "label": "ORG"}, {"text": "PDF", "label": "ORG"}, {"text": "Poisson", "label": "PERSON"}]
--------------------------------------- Input TXT -  show= doc
Correcting inner filter effects, a non multilinear tensor decomposition method.Among measurement used in analytical chemistry, fluorescence spectroscopy is widely spread and its applications are numerous. To recover various information on unknown components in chemical mixtures, multilinear tensor decomposition of multiway fluorescence spectra has proven extremely powerful. However, inner filter effects induce a systematic error on measurements, disturbing the decomposition. In this paper, we fully describe a non multilinear approach to include inner filter effects in the model instead of neglecting them or correcting them by linearization methods. A theoretical framework on non multilinear tensor decomposition is developed, an algorithm to recover the factors in the decomposition is detailed, and real data computer results are reported.

(ORG_The_VIMOS_Public_Extragalactic_Redshift_Survey VIPERS). Measuring nonlinear galaxy bias at z~0.8.We use the first release of of ORG_the_VImos_Public_Extragalactic_Redshift_Survey galaxies (VIPERS) of ~50,000 objects to measure the biasing relation between galaxies and mass in the redshift range z=[0.5,1.1]. We estimate the 1-point distribution function [] ORG_PDF of VIPERS galaxies from counts in cells and, assuming a model for the mass , ORG_PDF we infer their mean bias relation. The reconstruction of the bias relation from PDFs is performed through a novel method that accounts for noisePERSON_Poisson , redshift distortions, inhomogeneous sky coverage and other selection effects. With this procedure we constrain galaxy bias and its deviations from linearity down to scales as small as 4 Mpc/h and out to z=1.1. We detect small (~3%) but significant deviations from linear bias. The mean biasing function is close to linear in regions above the mean density. The mean slope of the biasing relation is a proxy to the linear bias parameter. It increases both with luminosity, in agreement with results of previous analyses, and with redshift. However, we detect a strong bias evolution only for in GPE_z>0.9 agreement with some, but not all, previous studies. We also detected a significant increase of the bias with the scale, from 4 to 8 Mpc/h, now seen for the first time out to z=1. The amplitude of nonlinearity depends on redshift, luminosity and on scales but no clear trend is detected. Thanks to the large cosmic volume probed by VIPERS we find that the mismatch between the previous estimates of bias at z~1 from zCOSMOS and VVDS-Deep galaxy samples is fully accounted for by cosmic variance. The results of our work confirm the importance of going beyond the over-simplistic linear bias hypothesis showing that non-linearities can be accurately measured through the applications of the appropriate statistical tools to existing datasets like VIPERS.

MX_Correcting MX_inner MX_filter effects, a non multilinear MX_tensor decomposition MX_method .Among measurement MX_used in analytical chemistry, fluorescence spectroscopy is widely MX_spread and its applications are numerous. To recover various information on unknown components in chemical mixtures, multilinear MX_tensor decomposition of multiway fluorescence spectra has proven extremely powerful. However, MX_inner MX_filter effects induce a systematic MX_error on measurements, disturbing the decomposition. In this MX_paper , we fully describe a non multilinear approach to include MX_inner MX_filter effects in the MX_model instead of MX_neglecting them or MX_correcting them by linearization MX_methods . A theoretical MX_framework on non multilinear MX_tensor decomposition is MX_developed , an MX_algorithm to recover the MX_factors in the decomposition is detailed, and real MX_data MX_computer MX_results are MX_reported .

The VIMOS Public Extragalactic Redshift Survey (VIPERS). Measuring MX_nonlinear galaxy MX_bias at z~0.8.We MX_use the first release of the VImos Public Extragalactic Redshift Survey of galaxies (VIPERS) of ~50,000 MX_objects to measure the biasing relation between galaxies and MX_mass in the MX_redshift range z=[0.5,1.1]. We estimate the 1-point distribution MX_function [PDF] of VIPERS galaxies from MX_counts in MX_cells and, assuming a MX_model for the MX_mass PDF, we MX_infer their mean MX_bias relation. The reconstruction of the MX_bias relation from PDFs is MX_performed through a novel MX_method that MX_accounts for Poisson noise, MX_redshift distortions, inhomogeneous MX_sky coverage and other selection effects. With this procedure we constrain galaxy MX_bias and its deviations from linearity down to MX_scales as MX_small as 4 Mpc/h and out to z=1.1. We MX_detect MX_small (~3%) but significant deviations from MX_linear MX_bias . The mean biasing MX_function is close to MX_linear in MX_regions above the mean density. The mean MX_slope of the MX_biasing relation is a proxy to the MX_linear MX_bias MX_parameter . It increases both with luminosity, in MX_agreement with MX_results of previous analyses, and with MX_redshift . However, we MX_detect a MX_strong MX_bias evolution only for z>0.9 in MX_agreement with some, but not all, previous studies. We also MX_detected a significant increase of the MX_bias with the MX_scale , from 4 to 8 Mpc/h, now MX_seen for the first MX_time out to z=1. The amplitude of nonlinearity MX_depends on MX_redshift , luminosity and on MX_scales but no clear MX_trend is MX_detected . Thanks to the large cosmic volume MX_probed by VIPERS we find that the MX_mismatch between the previous estimates of MX_bias at z~1 from zCOSMOS and VVDS-Deep galaxy samples is fully MX_accounted for by cosmic variance. The MX_results of our MX_work confirm the importance of going beyond the over-simplistic MX_linear MX_bias hypothesis MX_showing that non-linearities MX_can be accurately measured through the applications of the appropriate statistical MX_tools to existing datasets like VIPERS.
